<TD VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><FONT COLOR="#ffffff"><B><FONT COLOR="#ffffff">ENERGY FACTOR</FONT></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:2pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:1pt" align="left">&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE CELLSPACING="0" CELLPADDING="0" WIDTH="100%" BORDER="0" STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" ALIGN="center">

<TD WIDTH="100%"></TD></TR>


<TR STYLE="page-break-inside:avoid ; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">
<TD VALIGN="bottom" STYLE="BORDER:1px solid #000000; padding-left:8pt; padding-right:2pt"> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:1.00em; text-indent:-1.00em; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>HERO
IMAGE:</U></B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:4pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">


<IMG SRC="g101787g0429230030444.jpg" ALT="LOGO">
</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:1pt">&nbsp;</P></TD></TR>
</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Title: MIT&#146;s Drake Hernandez sees a future with hydrogen solutions </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Exploring potential energy solutions through systems modeling </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">First-generation college graduate Drake Hernandez is clearing a path for young engineers looking to enter the ever-changing energy industry, while also finding
the way to achieve a lower-carbon <U>future</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Raised 15 miles from ExxonMobil&#146;s&nbsp;<U>chemical plant</U>&nbsp;in Beaumont, Texas, Drake never
thought he&#146;d work in the energy industry that surrounded his hometown. But today, he is a graduate student at the Massachusetts Institute of Technology (MIT). Drake&#146;s research includes assisting a team with the development of a tool known
as <U>Sustainable Energy System Analysis Modeling</U>, or SESAME. The tool can project the net emissions of different energy solutions and the costs associated with deploying cutting-edge energy technologies. Specifically within this tool, Drake
analyzes the hydrogen value chain and regulations surrounding the emerging hydrogen market. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Hydrogen fuel, an energy carrier derived from either natural
gas or splitting water molecules, has the potential to help industrial processes achieve lower emissions, power commercial vehicles at scale, and heat homes without producing any carbon emissions. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Drake recently <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-led</FONT> the planning and execution of the MIT Energy Conference, a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">three-day</FONT> virtual event that drew over 800 attendees who ranged from students to energy sector executives. Joined by leading voices from academia, industry, and public service &#151; including former Secretary
of Energy, Ernst Moniz and former U.S. Senator from North Dakota, Heidi Heitkamp &#151; the conference explored the progress and challenges of navigating the energy transition. Vice President of ExxonMobil R&amp;D, Vijay Swarup, also participated on
a panel. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Drake took time from this work to talk about his perspective on hydrogen technology and how it may play a role in an alternative energy mosaic
to reduce emissions in the future. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>The future of hydrogen energy: A Q&amp;A with Drake Hernandez </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Energy Factor (EF):</B>&nbsp;Thank you, Drake, for taking the time to talk to us today. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Drake Hernandez (DH):</B>&nbsp;Of course. Thank you for having me. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;What initially drew you to the energy industry? </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;I grew up in a small town called Groves, Texas, which is really not far from Exxon&#146;s Beaumont plant. I spent 18 years there amidst the
lights of refineries and chemical plants, but, ultimately, I ended up at the University of Texas at Austin (UT) &#150; dubbed the &#147;energy university.&#148; Energy was ubiquitous there, so I really fell into it. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">I am a first-generation college student. I wanted to explore beyond my hometown after graduating high school. I was fortunate to receive a scholarship to UT,
so I found my way up to Austin. I guess I wasn&#146;t done running yet, because I then went up to Boston and worked there for a couple years as a consultant in the energy sector before moving even farther north, if you will, just across the river to
Cambridge. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At the end of the day, energy touches everything, and it was the area where I thought I could have the most impact. Going into school as a
mechanical engineer, I initially thought I wanted to design golf clubs for a living, but I quickly realized that I wanted to do something that had a bit more impact for human beings and society at large. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;The energy sector is in a period of transition right now. As a young engineer, do you see a way to deliver more energy with fewer emissions?
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;I&#146;m a graduate student at MIT now with the MIT Energy Initiative (MITEI) and what that means is I am inherently a techno-optimist.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You&#146;re absolutely right, we are going to have to provide more energy while simultaneously curbing emissions. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Technological advances working alongside strategically-designed policy and regulatory measures are going to be critical to meeting this goal. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;Can you talk a bit about your work with the life cycle assessment tool? Why is it particularly important for decision makers today? </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;Yeah. The tool you&#146;re referring to is the Sustainable Energy System Analysis Modeling Environment, or SESAME. This is a tool that&#146;s
been developed to analyze the life cycle emissions associated with any energy pathway and is currently being expanded to evaluate cost impacts associated with each of these pathways. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">First, SESAME can model emissions reductions associated with deploying certain technologies. For example, if you&#146;re thinking, &#147;Alright, I&#146;m
making investments in new energy technologies. What does this actually mean from a <U>carbon emissions</U> perspective?&#148; Then, it&#146;s likely that you&#146;ll want to compare, for instance, the carbon intensity of producing one kilowatt-hour
of electricity from wind power, to the carbon intensity of producing one kilowatt-hour from natural gas. It&#146;s critical to have a tool like this, especially in the hands of policy makers or investors these days, as they seek a better
understanding of how to achieve their environmental or sustainability goals. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The next aspect of SESAME is the cost analysis portion. So now, not only do
you have the projected carbon emissions associated with a specific energy system, but also the economic implications. This is going to be critical. In concert with the actual carbon emissions data, the economic analyses of this tool will yield a
very powerful framework that&#146;s hopefully used around the world as people look to eliminate emissions from their energy systems. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;And what got you interested in hydrogen specifically? </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;Hydrogen has numerous applications within the energy space. It can serve to reduce emissions in a wide variety of sectors within our economy.
However, it&#146;s important to realize the production of hydrogen is not necessarily clean today. Lower-carbon hydrogen production technologies &#151; like electrolyzers, which split water molecules into pure hydrogen and oxygen, or pairing carbon
capture with steam methane reforming assets solutions &#151; are going to be important and it&#146;s going to take all of these different technologies working in concert to achieve the transformative effort. The development of a hydrogen market
could also drive the new business models. And I personally think that this will drive cost reductions. And, as hydrogen becomes cheaper, it&#146;s going to become more economically competitive for a number of end uses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;What do you think the public should know about hydrogen as an energy source? </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;The key takeaway is that hydrogen is not a silver bullet. Especially over the last year or so, there&#146;s been a big hype wave around
hydrogen where people think it can solve everything; but it shouldn&#146;t be thought of that way. You should be using it strategically, because it is a valuable resource. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">There are definitely going to be applications where hydrogen is the best and most cost-effective way to reduce emissions and the best application for a
particular end use. However, it&#146;s not meant to be used everywhere. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;That said, can you give an estimated guess as to how long it
could take before hydrogen becomes a force on the energy market? </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;I&#146;m going to give the classic economist answer which is, it
depends. One of my other key areas of research focuses on regulatory issues that need to be addressed before hydrogen pipelines are developed en masse in the U.S. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">There are a few hydrogen pipelines that have been developed in the Gulf Coast area, connecting refineries and chemical plants. But if you get this pipeline
infrastructure built out on a larger scale, realistically, your delivered cost of hydrogen is going to decrease quite substantially. So I think regulation is going to be the driver of market development. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;By &#147;regulation&#148; you mean infrastructure and national support for it? </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;Exactly. When you look at building a natural gas pipeline in the US right now, there&#146;s a defined process associated with developing the
infrastructure and there&#146;s a regulatory accounting framework. No such process exists for hydrogen infrastructure today because it is so new and it&#146;s a fundamentally different energy commodity. My Master&#146;s thesis is focused
substantially on this. In particular, I evaluate different regulatory frameworks the federal government could pursue to stimulate investment in interstate hydrogen transmission infrastructure. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;Finally, with everything that you&#146;ve seen and all the work that you&#146;re doing, where would you like to be in 10 years,
professionally? </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DH:</B>&nbsp;I just want to have an impact. We&#146;re in a critical time right now as a species, traversing the energy transition
with a massive capital deployment between now and 2050. At this point, I&#146;m just trying to do whatever I can to be an element for positive change in driving carbon reduction, be that working for an energy company as they develop corporate
strategies or working for governments as they look to develop and design markets for electric power or hydrogen or whatever around the world to enable this effort. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>EF:</B>&nbsp;Lots of exciting and significant challenges, I would say. Thank you very much. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Learn more about the renewable energy landscape and how ExxonMobil is positioning for a <U>lower-carbon future</U>. </I></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt" ALIGN="center">


<IMG SRC="g101787snap2.jpg" ALT="LOGO">

The Texas native discusses his education, career, and why he&#146;s optimistic about the future of energy.</P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
